  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_c2b23c90-ecda-4106-8a6b-da17da91c9b0'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

<span id="freeTextContainer3668825684731509871">Reading goes to the dogs in this timeless Beginner Book edited by Dr. Seuss. From big dogs and little dogs to red, green, and blue dogs, dogs going up and dogs going fast . . . who knew dogs were so busy?   <span id="freeText3668825684731509871" style="display:none">Reading goes to the dogs in this timeless Beginner Book edited by Dr. Seuss. From big dogs and little dogs to red, green, and blue dogs, dogs going up and dogs going fast . . . who knew dogs were so busy? And laughter will ensue at the repeated question “Do you like my hat?” Like P. D. Eastman’s classic <i>Are You My Mother?</i> <i>Go, Dog. Go!</i> has been a go-to favorite for over fifty years, leaving audiences of all breeds wagging their tails with delight.<br /><br /><br /> Originally created by Dr. Seuss, Beginner Books encourage children to read all by themselves, with simple words and illustrations that give clues to their meaning.<br /><br /> "The canine cartoons make an elementary text funny and coherent and still one of the best around."--<i>School Library Journal.  <br /></i></span>

<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">I have a copy in the same size format from about 1991 that cost $7.99. I have a larger format of on Beyond Zebra so I presume this exists for Go, Dog <a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">I have a copy in the same size format from about 1991 that cost $7.99. I have a larger format of on Beyond Zebra so I presume this exists for Go, Dog Go! This was my favorite book of all for many years. I remember it being bigger but that memory may have just been me being smaller.<br /><a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

<div id="review_521352625" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/521352625" />
    <a title="Patrick" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/922495-patrick"><img alt="Patrick" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1351307095p2/922495.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/521352625?book_show_action=true">Jan 30, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Patrick" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Patrick" href="/user/show/922495-patrick">Patrick</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/922495-patrick?shelf=good-books-for-little-kids">good-books-for-little-kids</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/922495-patrick?shelf=talking-a-lot-of-shit">talking-a-lot-of-shit</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer521352625" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer543672814107269067"><br/>I know this is a classic and all, but I had a hard time making it through this book. It's full of needless repetition, which makes it longer than it needs to be. What's more, the plot is a mess, leaping from event to event almost randomly at times. <br/><br/>I respect what the author is attempting to do here, thematically. Eastman is asking bold questions about how things are related to one another. Are we a green dog or a yellow one? Is it day or night? These are big questions, and they need to be asked.</span>
  <span id="freeText543672814107269067" style="display:none"><br />I know this is a classic and all, but I had a hard time making it through this book. It's full of needless repetition, which makes it longer than it needs to be. What's more, the plot is a mess, leaping from event to event almost randomly at times. <br /><br />I respect what the author is attempting to do here, thematically. Eastman is asking bold questions about how things are related to one another. Are we a green dog or a yellow one? Is it day or night? These are big questions, and they need to be asked. <br /><br />That said, you can have a book that contains big ideas AND an interesting story too. And, unfortunately, the story is severely lacking here. <br /><br />The one saving grace of the book was the "Do you like my hat?" subplot, which was very tight in its execution and satisfying in its resolution. <br /><br />Ultimately, when reading a book like this, the question you have to ask yourself is "Would I buy the sequel?" And I have to say, with some regret, that I wouldn't. There were just too many structural problems with the story for that. <br /><br />* * *<br /><br />Seriously though, I had a great time reading this book with my little boy. Lots of basic words used in different situations make it a great tool. If I was still teaching ESL students, I would use this to clue in struggling students about prepositions. (If you think prepositions are easy, it's only because you're a native speaker. Try explaining to someone from Japan why you get *in* a car but *on* a train.) <br /><br />As a bonus, this book is long. Most kids books seem to be about 20 pages these days, but this is pretty easily triple that. It makes it less of a mind-numbing experience when you end up reading it a couple times. <br /><br />P.S. I meant what I said about the hat subplot. Genius. <br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="543672814107269067" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/123910211" />
    <a title="Matthew Rappelt" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3702580-matthew-rappelt"><img alt="Matthew Rappelt" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" /></a>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/123910211?book_show_action=true">Sep 28, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Matthew Rappelt" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Matthew Rappelt" href="/user/show/3702580-matthew-rappelt">Matthew Rappelt</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer123910211" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10330316926715458121">Truly, nothing has captured the scope of emotion that encompasses Romance such as Go Dog. Go! Part tragedy, part romantic comedy this is a love story for the ages. With such memorable wit and dialog such as the belly laugh inducing "Do you like my hat?" and the heart wrenching reply, "No I do not." You will laugh, and you'll cry. It's not all romance though, the book deftly weaves in several subplots which serve as complex metaphors for various political and philosophical debates. For example, t</span>
  <span id="freeText10330316926715458121" style="display:none">Truly, nothing has captured the scope of emotion that encompasses Romance such as Go Dog. Go! Part tragedy, part romantic comedy this is a love story for the ages. With such memorable wit and dialog such as the belly laugh inducing "Do you like my hat?" and the heart wrenching reply, "No I do not." You will laugh, and you'll cry. It's not all romance though, the book deftly weaves in several subplots which serve as complex metaphors for various political and philosophical debates. For example, there is a seen in which "The dogs go to sleep. They will sleep all night." is clearly an *obvious* metaphor for female hegemony towards the oppressive male dominated society of the early Mad Men era 1960's in which this book takes place. In other portions of the book it explores how the effects of how economic success and failure in the brewing industry plays out among moderate Democratic congressmen, for example "The blue dog is in. The red dog is out. (Clearly a throwback to Prohibitionist sentiment and history.)<br />At it's climax, Go, Dog. Go! explores how runaway consumerism, and out-of-control automobile industry have set American society on a one way path to self annihilation. Not even the power of the newly formed Green Movement can help society. The Green Movement(here symbolized by a Giant Tree), is consumed and polluted by society in a hedonistic Tree-Dog-Party. In the end we are teased with one ray of hope, as the male and female protagonists escape this debauchery together, their budding romance at long last blossomed, providing hope that someday through the verisimilitude of their mutual affection a new generation will be born that can overcome the pettiness of their forefathers, and set society on the path to salvation. </span>
  <a data-text-id="10330316926715458121" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1040589809" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2856240536809290556">Since the school year started, I've been forced to read this to (<i>or, more accurately, read along with</i>) my daughter...about 4 million times.<br/>Ok. Maybe I'm exaggerating.<br/>She's a BIG girl now, so they have to read for 15 minutes every day after school, which I think is GREAT!<br/><i>Except for the part where I have to listen to this story, and others like it, for the rest of the school year.</i><br/>Yes, the end result (hopefully, a literate child) is totally worth it.<br/>And for whatever reason, <b>Go, Dog. Go!</b> has become </span>
  <span id="freeText2856240536809290556" style="display:none">Since the school year started, I've been forced to read this to (<i>or, more accurately, read along with</i>) my daughter...about 4 million times.<br />Ok. Maybe I'm exaggerating.<br />She's a BIG girl now, so they have to read for 15 minutes every day after school, which I think is GREAT!<br /><i>Except for the part where I have to listen to this story, and others like it, for the rest of the school year.</i><br />Yes, the end result (hopefully, a literate child) is totally worth it.<br />And for whatever reason, <b>Go, Dog. Go!</b> has become her favorite choice for this assignment.<br /><br />The great thing about this one is the repetitive use of sight words that every kid needs to be able to quickly recognize.<br />For that reason alone, this thing is worth its weight in gold for beginning readers.<br />Then, of course, it has wacky dogs doing wacky dog things.<br />Can't go wrong with that, can you?<br />Not if you're a kid!<br /><br />My favorite part of the book is the Two Dogs and the Hat stuff.<br />No, it's not exactly comedy gold, but my daughter always does this funny little high-pitched voice for the girl dog, and a low (which still sounds squeaky coming from her) <i>manly</i> voice for the boy dog.<br />It's adorable.<br />Then again, I'm probably just biased. <br /><br />If you've got a little kid who's learning how to read, go get this sucker.<br />Sure, you'll be ready to tear your hair out after a few readings, but they'll love it. <br />It's called <b>sacrifice</b>. Now suck it up, and grab this for your kid.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2856240536809290556" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

Overall, I found the overarching message of this masterpiece insightful and full of ethically sound judgments.   <span id="freeText2665785164057480362" style="display:none">When I first met Erika, for some long forgotten reason and situation, someone said, "Do you like my hat?"<br /><br />I answered: "No. I do not." There was an awkward pause and I added, "Good-bye. Good-bye again," with some totally bizarre, guttural, kiddie voice. It became a fun inside joke for Erika and me, but for the life of us, we couldn't remember where it came from. It sounded familiar; it didn't sound me-invented, but we couldn't place it. <br /><br />Then we had babes, and I picked up a bunch of board books -- and there it was.<br /><br />"Hello!"<br /><br />"Hello!"<br /><br />"Do you like my hat?"<br /><br />"I do not."<br /><br />"Good-by."<br /><br />"Good-by."<br /><br />It wasn't quite how I remembered it, not quite the way my mind had twisted it over all those years, but we had finally found the source, and we were stoked. <br /><br />5 years later my boy is reading it to me. It is a great book to foster reading , but even if I didn't have a prior bond with the book beyond learning to read, I would still love <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/460548.Go__Dog__Go___Beginner_Books_R__" title="Go, Dog. Go! (Beginner Books(R)) by P.D. Eastman" rel="nofollow noopener">Go Dog. Go</a> because of my son.<br /><br />It is a fave. No question. </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer3905037234986309398">This book gave me troubles in pre-school. It must have been some kind of Montessori situation, I'm not sure.   <span id="freeText3905037234986309398" style="display:none">This book gave me troubles in pre-school. It must have been some kind of Montessori situation, I'm not sure. If I could read well then I was allowed into the room with all of the books (including this one, which I more or less wanted to read every day), but nap-time was governed by some awful person who did not rub backs. I was forced to choose between pretending to be dull but receiving back rubs and giving up back rubs but being allowed to read GDG every day). Such was my introduction to the imperfections of this world.</span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer203924954" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer8952089295681842946">This is my all time favorite book to read to my kids, even down to the size of the book. It uses some tricky moves to get children to learn, and its an incredible story without being a story. <br/><br/>Why is one dog still wide awake with his big, white eyes when the rest are asleep? What is he thinking about? And is this the same dog who is asleep when it is time for the dogs to get up? And how about playing checkers on the boat while your buddy plays guitar? Dreamy. And the poor bird crossing the street</span>
  <span id="freeText8952089295681842946" style="display:none">This is my all time favorite book to read to my kids, even down to the size of the book. It uses some tricky moves to get children to learn, and its an incredible story without being a story. <br /><br />Why is one dog still wide awake with his big, white eyes when the rest are asleep? What is he thinking about? And is this the same dog who is asleep when it is time for the dogs to get up? And how about playing checkers on the boat while your buddy plays guitar? Dreamy. And the poor bird crossing the street that makes all the dogs Screech on their brakes. What was he thinking and where was he going? And finally, "Do you like my hat?" I randomly ask my kids that question intermittently and they always know exactly how to answer.<br /><br />By the way, anybody notice that the dog steals the feather out of the female dogs hat at one point? yes, its true. First she has the feather in her hat, then he seems to have snatched it.<br /><br />The Dog party at the end is like an opium dream. This must be the true dog heaven. I want to be reincarnated as a dog and star in Go Dog Go.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8952089295681842946" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <a title="Kat" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1008175-kat"><img alt="Kat" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1370231937p2/1008175.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/684751534?book_show_action=true">Aug 03, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kat" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kat" href="/user/show/1008175-kat">Kat</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1008175-kat?shelf=picture-books">picture-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1008175-kat?shelf=2013">2013</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer684751534" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8661483738757662040">Basic plot: Dogs doing things!<br/><br/>I know it isn't really a plot, but the book doesn't really have one. This book uses simple repetition and clear pictures to teach kids about prepositions (under, over, in, on, etc), sizes, and a few other basic concepts. The pictures are funny and have lots of details to talk about with little ones beyond the words on the page. There's a lot of good repeat factor in there because of this. I took this book on a 2-week vacation with my 5-year old and read it almost ev</span>
  <span id="freeText8661483738757662040" style="display:none">Basic plot: Dogs doing things!<br /><br />I know it isn't really a plot, but the book doesn't really have one. This book uses simple repetition and clear pictures to teach kids about prepositions (under, over, in, on, etc), sizes, and a few other basic concepts. The pictures are funny and have lots of details to talk about with little ones beyond the words on the page. There's a lot of good repeat factor in there because of this. I took this book on a 2-week vacation with my 5-year old and read it almost every night, picking a different page to describe more fully each night. It's also a much longer book than a lot of other picture books designed for kids. It keeps attention, though, reminding us adults that kids can have an attention span beyond a few seconds if the text is worthwhile! A few older-than-me (60-something) campmates seemed quite tickled that this book was still being read. There is a reason why Eastman ranks up with Seuss in staying power of the books written. :) Those books are quality stuff that every child should read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8661483738757662040" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_193713959" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/193713959" />
    <a title="Jessica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5813983-jessica"><img alt="Jessica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1310862480p2/5813983.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/193713959?book_show_action=true">Aug 02, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jessica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jessica" href="/user/show/5813983-jessica">Jessica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer193713959" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16928787711563629554">My Dad read so many books to me, but this is one of the few that I remember. I still remember puzzling about what was so much better about the girl dog's hat at the end? I thought it was the ugliest hat she'd worn so far! <br/>The illustrations of the dogs sleeping were very thought-provoking to me as well. I wondered why the one dog didn't have its eyes open. Was it sleeping with its eyes open, or staying awake all night? Why did it say,"they will sleep all night", when obviously at least one of the</span>
  <span id="freeText16928787711563629554" style="display:none">My Dad read so many books to me, but this is one of the few that I remember. I still remember puzzling about what was so much better about the girl dog's hat at the end? I thought it was the ugliest hat she'd worn so far! <br />The illustrations of the dogs sleeping were very thought-provoking to me as well. I wondered why the one dog didn't have its eyes open. Was it sleeping with its eyes open, or staying awake all night? Why did it say,"they will sleep all night", when obviously at least one of them was awake. Were the ones under the bed really asleep?<br />I remember always wanting to be IN the cars myself. and sitting under the tree, and oh, I wanted to live in that houseboat!<br />The dog party looked fun, but a little scary too. How did they keep from falling down?<br />Best of all, I got to sit in my Dad's lap and hear him make voices for the different dogs. Thank you P.D. Eastman.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16928787711563629554" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('BPEX96l9Rmybw/e/u+mVnZOFmpFFHF68cM0gEjeeCgO7aX/Rs/UpdIYQIlFORCyAn7aYEgbMfnh8g4DRg6LRUQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('zeFvl0vFxl89mdMZHaAACvxy+ZsRpN2/0aRsLaCycnNyeQexUU2pRyBKBvfoDbkX8EH7GFJ0/Xvd6szuFI6pIQ==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer8114685728657481462">Philip Dey "Phil" Eastman was an American screenwriter, children's author, and illustrator. As an author, he is known primarily as P. D. Eastman. A protégé of Theodor Geisel (Dr. Seuss), Eastman wrote many books for children, in his own distinct style under the Dr. Seuss brand of Random House, many of which were in the Beginner Books series. <br/><br/>From 1936 to 1941, Eastman worked at the story departmen</span>
  <span id="freeText8114685728657481462" style="display:none">Philip Dey "Phil" Eastman was an American screenwriter, children's author, and illustrator. As an author, he is known primarily as P. D. Eastman. A protégé of Theodor Geisel (Dr. Seuss), Eastman wrote many books for children, in his own distinct style under the Dr. Seuss brand of Random House, many of which were in the Beginner Books series. <br /><br />From 1936 to 1941, Eastman worked at the story department of Walt Disney Productions. From 1941 to 1943 he worked at the story department of Warner Bros. Cartoons. From 1945 to 1952 he worked in the story department of United Productions of America. He contributed to the "Private Snafu" World War II training films, wrote for the animation Mr. Magoo, and the Gerald McBoing-Boing series for UPA.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8114685728657481462" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
